## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology (population dynamics / growth models)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is the time-derivative of population size P, indicating a dynamical systems formulation of population growth. Typical relationships encode per-capita growth, density dependence (crowding/carrying capacity), Allee effects, harvesting, and environmental/seasonal forcing via t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited resources; constant per-capita rate)
- Linear birth–death with baseline influx/outflux: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 (net proportional growth plus constant source/sink)
- Quadratic crowding (self-limitation): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (pairwise competition; simplest density dependence)
- Logistic differential form (Verhulst): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (growth reduced linearly by density; carrying capacity ~ 1/c1)
- Ricker-type continuous density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(-c1 * P) (per-capita rate decreases approximately exponentially with density)
- Gompertz-type growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / (P + c2)) (logarithmic density dependence; slowing growth near an upper bound)
- Theta-logistic (generalized logistic ODE): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (nonlinear density dependence; adjustable crowding curvature)
- Richards-type generalized logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2)**c3 (additional shape parameter controlling asymmetry of approach to capacity)
- Strong Allee effect with carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (negative growth below an Allee threshold; saturation at high P)
- Harvesting/removal with density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (proportional harvesting or mortality on top of logistic growth)
- Constant-yield harvesting with crowding: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (constant extraction; extinction possible if too large)
- Time-varying intrinsic rate (trend): dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (environmental change causing growth rate to drift over time)
- Seasonally forced growth: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (periodic environment affecting per-capita rate)
- Seasonally forced logistic: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P * (1 - c4 * P) (seasonality plus density dependence)
- Time-varying carrying capacity proxy: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P / (c2 + c3 * exp(c4 * t))) (resource/capacity changes over time; crowding scaled by a time-varying factor)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Proportionality to P (dP_dt ∝ P) indicates constant per-capita growth/decay (density-independent dynamics).
- A negative P**2 term (or P*(1 - c*P)) represents crowding/competition where per-capita growth declines roughly linearly with density.
- Factors like (1 - (c*P)**a) imply nonlinear density dependence: a > 1 creates sharper suppression near high P; a < 1 creates earlier suppression.
- Log terms such as P*log(c/(P+c)) encode Gompertz-like regulation where relative growth slows approximately with log-population, often fitting asymmetric sigmoids.
- An exp(-c*P) multiplier implies strong density-dependent inhibition where additional individuals rapidly reduce per-capita growth (overcompensation-like behavior).
- A factor (c*P - 1) (or (P - A)) indicates an Allee threshold: growth is negative below a critical population size.
- Additive negative constants (e.g., -c) model constant-yield harvesting; combined with density dependence they create extinction thresholds/bistability.
- Sin(c*t + φ) or other periodic functions of t capture seasonality/forcing; when multiplied by P they represent seasonally varying per-capita rates.
- Time-dependent coefficients (c0 + c1*t, exp(c*t)) reflect gradual environmental change; they can produce accelerating/declining growth regimes even without density terms.

- **Candidate 1**: Has (P+1)^(1/4) and sin terms. Set c2=0 (kills exp term), c4=0 (kills sin term). Left with c0*P^(1/3) + c1*P + (P+1)^(1/4) - 1. The (P+1)^(1/4) can't become P². **NO MATCH**

- **Candidate 3**: c0*P^(1/3) + c1*P + c2*log(c3*P+1) + c4*exp(c5*P)*log(c6*P+1). No P². Set c4=0, c2=0: just c0*P^(1/3)+c1*P. Missing P². **NO MATCH**

- **Candidate 4**: c0*P^(1/3) + c1*P + c2*sin(c3*P+c4) + c5*exp(c6*P). Set c2=0, c5=0: no P². **NO MATCH**

- **Candidate 5**: Similar, no P² source. **NO MATCH**

- **Candidate 6**: No P² source. **NO MATCH**

- **Candidate 7**: No P² source. **NO MATCH**

- **Candidate 8**: Has (P+1)^(1/4). No P² source. **NO MATCH**

- **Candidate 9**: c0*P^(1/3) + c1*P + c2*P*(c3*P+1)*(c4*P-1) + c5*log(c6*P+1)*cos(c7*P). The cubic term: c2*P*(c3*c4*P²+(c4-c3)*P-1) = c2*c3*c4*P³ + c2*(c4-c3)*P² - c2*P. This has P³ which can't be eliminated without losing P². Set c5=0. Then c0*P^(1/3) + (c1-c2)*P + c2*(c4-c3)*P² + c2*c3*c4*P³. Need c2*c3*c4=0. If c4=0: c2*(-c3)*P² - c2*P. So: c0*P^(1/3) + (c1-c2)*P - c2*c3*P² ✓ **MATCH**

- **Candidate 10**: No P² source. **NO MATCH**

- **Candidate 11**: No P² source. **NO MATCH**

- **Candidate 12**: Has (P+1)^(1/4). No P². **NO MATCH**

- **Candidate 13**: No P² source. **NO MATCH**

- **Candidate 14**: Has (P+c7)^(1/4). No P². **NO MATCH**

- **Candidate 15**: (c0 + (c1*P+c2)*(c3*P^(1/3)+c4*P+c5*sin(c6*P+c7)))/(c1*P+c2). Set c5=0: c3*P^(1/3) + c4*P + c0/(c1*P+c2). The last term is rational, not polynomial. **NO MATCH** unless c0=0: then c3*P^(1/3)+c4*P. Missing P². **NO MATCH**

- **Candidate 16**: No P² source. **NO MATCH**

- **Candidate 17**: (c0*P^(1/3)*(c1*P+c2) + c3*P*(c1*P+c2) + c4*P + c5*(P+1)²*(c1*P+c2) + c6)/(c1*P+c2). = c0*P^(1/3) + c3*P + c4*P/(c1*P+c2) + c5*(P+1)² + c6/(c1*P+c2). The rational terms can't be polynomial. Set c4=0, c6=0: c0*P^(1/3) + c3*P + c5*(P²+2P+1) = c0*P^(1/3) + c5*P² + (c3+2*c5)*P + c5. Need c5=0 for no constant, but then no P². **NO MATCH** unless we accept constant... wait, GT has no constant term. If c5≠0, there's a constant c5 that can't be removed. **NO MATCH**

- **Candidate 18**: c0*P^(1/3) + c1 + c2*log(c3*exp(c4*P)+1). This is softplus-like. No P². **NO MATCH**

- **Candidate 20**: c0*P^(1/3) + c1*P + c2*P*(c3*P+1)*(c4*P-1) + c5*sin(c6*P). Same as candidate 9 analysis but with sin instead of log*cos. Set c5=0, c4=0: c0*P^(1/3) + (c1-c2)*P - c2*c3*P² ✓ **MATCH**

- **Candidate 21**: c0*P^(1/3) + c1*P³ + c2*P + c3*log(c4*P+1) + c5 + (P+c6)^(1/4). Set c1=0, c3=0: c0*P^(1/3) + c2*P + c5 + (P+c6)^(1/4). No P². **NO MATCH**

- **Candidate 22**: c0*(c1*P + c2 + c3*(c4*P^(1/3) + c5*P + c6*sin(c7*P+c8))). Set c6=0: c0*(c1*P + c2 + c3*c4*P^(1/3) + c3*c5*P) = c0*c3*c4*P^(1/3) + c0*(c1+c3*c5)*P + c0*c2. Has constant c0*c2. Set c2=0: c0*c3*c4*P^(1/3) + c0*(c1+c3*c5)*P. No P². **NO MATCH**

- **Candidate 23**: c0*P^(1/3) + P³ + c1*P + c2*P*(c3*P+1)*(c4*P-1). Expands to c0*P^(1/3) + P³ + c1*P + c2*c3*c4*P³ + ... Has P³ that can't be fully eliminated (the explicit P³ remains unless c2*c3*c4 = -1, but then other terms remain). Let me expand fully: c0*P^(1/3) + P³ + c1*P + c2*c3*c4*P³ + c2*(c4-c3)*P² - c2*P = c0*P^(1/3) + (1+c2*c3*c4)*P³ + c2*(c4-c3)*P² + (c1-c2)*P. Set 1+c2*c3*c4=0: then c2*c3*c4=-1. Still have c2*(c4-c3)*P² and (c1-c2)*P. This works! ✓ **MATCH**

- **Candidate 24**: c0*P^(1/3) + c1*P + c2*P*log(c3*P+1) + c4*log(c3*P+1). No P². **NO MATCH**

- **Candidate 29**: c0*P^(1/3) + c1*P + P + c2 + c3*log(c4*exp(c5*P)+1). No P². **NO MATCH**

- **Candidate 31**: c0*P^(1/3) + (c1+c2)*P + c3*log(c4*exp(c5*P)+1) + c6. No P². **NO MATCH**

- **Candidate 32**: No P². **NO MATCH**

- **Candidate 38**: Has t variable. Set c1=0: (c0*P^(1/3)*c2 + c3*P*c2 + c4*(P+1)²*c2 + c5*t + c6)/c2 = c0*P^(1/3) + c3*P + c4*(P+1)² + c5*t/c2 + c6/c2. Still has t. Set c5=0: c0*P^(1/3) + c3*P + c4*P² + 2*c4*P + c4 + c6/c2. Constant c4+c6/c2 must be 0 (achievable). Then c0*P^(1/3) + c4*P² + (c3+2*c4)*P ✓ **MATCH**

- **Candidate 43**: c0*P^(1/3) + c1*P³ + c2*P + c3*log(c4*|P|+1) + c5 + (P+c6)^(1/4). Set c1=0, c3=0: no P². **NO MATCH**

- **Candidate 59**: No P². **NO MATCH**

- **Candidate 60**: (c0*P + c1 + (c2*P+c3)*(c4*P^(1/3)+c5*P+c6*log(c7*exp(c8*P)+1)))/(c2*P+c3). Set c6=0: c4*P^(1/3) + c5*P + (c0*P+c1)/(c2*P+c3). Rational term not polynomial unless c0/c2 with remainder. Set c0=0, c1=0: c4*P^(1/3)+c5*P. No P². **NO MATCH**

- **Candidate 61**: No P². **NO MATCH**

- **Candidate 62**: No P². **NO MATCH**

- **Candidate 63**: No P². **NO MATCH**
